54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > SERVICE PRECAUTIONS
SERVICE PRECAUTIONS
Warnings in diagnosis sectionDetails regarding warning
cautionWhen servicing a CAN bus line, earth yourself by touching a metal object such as an unpainted water pipe. If you fail to do, a component connected to the CAN bus line may be broken.
-
cautionA digital multimeter should be used.
When measuring resistance value or voltage in CAN bus lines, use a digital multimeter. If not using a digital multimeter, the equipment, which are connected through the CAN communication lines, may be damaged.
cautionWhen measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Disconnect the negative battery terminal when measuring the resistance value in the CAN bus line. If you fail to do so, the equipment, which are connected through the CAN communication lines, may be damaged.
cautionThe test wiring harness should be used.
Always use the test harness when measuring the voltage or resistance value at the female connector. If you fail to do so, connectors may be damaged.
cautionThe strand end of the twist wire should be within 10 cm from the connector.
If you repair the wire due to a defective connector or its terminal or harness wire, you should cut the wire so that the strand end of the twist wire should be within 10 cm from the connector as shown. If it exceeds 10 cm, twist the wiring harness just like the original twisted wire. If the strand end exceeds 10 cm, a communication error may be caused.
cautionStrictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
When you repair a CAN bus line, observe the precautions on how to repair the CAN bus line strictly. Refer to . If a new wire is added or a splice point is modified for the CAN_L or CAN_H line, an error in the CAN communication may be caused.
54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > PRECAUTIONS ON HOW TO REPAIR THE CAN BUS LINES
PRECAUTIONS ON HOW TO REPAIR THE CAN BUS LINES
 
 
 
 
PRECAUTIONS ON HOW TO REPAIR THE CAN BUS LINES
  • If the CAN bus line(s) are repaired, renew all the twisted wires between the end connectors. If the wiring harness is partially repaired, or only CAN_L or CAN_H line is repaired, noise suppression is deteriorated, causing a communication error.
  • If the connector or wire on the main bus line or the sub-bus wire is replaced, the frayed end of the twisted wire should be within 10 cm from the connector. If it exceeds 10 cm, twist the wiring harness just like the original twisted wire. If the frayed end exceeds 10 cm, noise suppression is deteriorated, causing a communication error.
  • If a sub-bus line is repaired, splice a new wire directly into the main bus line. If a new wire is spliced into the sub-bus line, which is connected to another device, the CAN communication will be disabled.
 
 
PRECAUTIONS ON HOW TO REPAIR THE TERMINATOR RESISTOR
If one-side terminator resistor is broken, the CAN communication will continue although noise suppression is deteriorated. No diagnosis codes may be set even if the terminator resistor was broken. If a damage is found, replace the ECU which incorporates the defective terminator resistor.
 
 
CAN BUS LINE REPAIR HARNESS (PART NAME AND NUMBER)
Part namePart number
Twist pair cableMN151514
54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > EXPLANATION ABOUT THE M.U.T.-III CAN BUS DIAGNOSTICS
EXPLANATION ABOUT THE M.U.T.-III CAN BUS DIAGNOSTICS
 
 
The M.U.T.-III CAN bus diagnostics carries out the 3 checks below automatically, and then displays current condition of the CAN bus lines according to the check results.
 
 
CAN BUS LINE DIAGNOSTIC FLOW
1. M.U.T.-III CAN bus diagnostics
The M.U.T.-III diagnoses CAN bus lines in accordance with the following strategy.
  • Checking the communication condition of ECUs
    The M.U.T.-III narrows down troubles in circuit by itself. Its strategies are as follows.
ECU which cannot communicate with the M.U.T.-IIIPossible trouble spotLogic for narrowing down trouble spot
ECU ACAN bus line (a) and power supply system to ECU AECU A communicates with the M.U.T.-III via CAN bus lines (a) and (b). The M.U.T.-III judges that CAN bus line (b) is normal, because it can communicate with other ECUs. Possible trouble may be present in CAN bus line (a) or the power supply system to ECU A.
ECU CCAN bus line (g) and power supply system to ECU CECU C communicates with the M.U.T.-III via CAN bus lines (b), (c), (d) and (g). The M.U.T.-III judges that CAN bus lines (b), (c) and (d) are normal, because it can communicate with ECUs B and D. Possible trouble may be present in CAN bus line (g) or the power supply system to ECU C.
ECU C and ECU DTrouble in CAN bus line (d)ECUs C ad D communicate with the M.U.T.-III via CAN bus lines (b), (c), (d), (e) and (g). The M.U.T.-III judges that CAN bus lines (b) and (c) are normal, because it can communicate with ECU B. Possible trouble may be present in CAN bus line (d), (e) or (g) or the power supply system to ECU D or C. CAN bus line (d) is shared by ECUs C and D when they communicate with the M.U.T.-III, so CAN bus line (d) is suspected as ultimate cause. CAN bus line (g) or (e) and power supply systems to ECU C or D are also suspected as second cause.
ECU B and ECU DCAN bus line (e) or (f) or power supply system to ECU B or DECUs B ad D communicate with the M.U.T.-III via CAN bus lines (b), (c), (d), (e) and (f). The M.U.T.-III judges that CAN bus lines (b), (c) and (d) are normal, because it can communicate with ECU C. Possible trouble may be present in CAN bus line (f) or (e) or the power supply system to ECU B or D.
2. If diagnosis code related to CAN communication is set as past trouble, isolate opens as described below.
noteIf you pinpoint trouble spot according to diagnosis code, you should use time-out diagnosis code. diagnosis code related to failure information is set when the data to be set contains an error, so CAN bus line itself is probably normal.
noteTime-out diagnosis codes are stored in each ECU memory individually. Therefore, it is possible that these diagnosis codes have not been set simultaneously. If the trouble spot cannot be found when you diagnose by judging from multiple diagnosis codes, check the communication lines between each ECU.
Diagnosis code to be setPossible trouble spotLogic for narrowing down trouble spot
Time-out diagnosis code associated with ECU D is stored in ECU A, ECU B and ECU C.Trouble in CAN bus line (e) and power supply system to ECU DWhen time-out diagnosis code associated with ECU D is stored in ECU A, B and C, or time-out diagnosis code associated with ECUs A, B and C is stored in ECU D, CAN bus line (e) is suspected. When diagnosis code is not stored in ECU D, the power supply to ECU D is suspected.
Time-out diagnosis code associated with ECUs A, B, C and D is stored in ECU.
Time-out diagnosis code associated with ECU A is stored in ECUs B, C and D.Trouble in CAN bus line (a) or (c) and power supply system to ECU A.When time-out diagnosis code associated with ECU A is stored in ECUs B, C and D, or time-out diagnosis code associated with ECUs B, C and D is stored in ECU A, CAN bus line (a) or (c) is suspected. When diagnosis code is not stored in ECU A, the power supply to ECU A is suspected.
Time-out diagnosis code associated with ECUs B, C and D is stored in ECU A.
Time-out diagnosis codes associated with ECUs C and D are stored in ECU A and ECU B.Trouble in CAN bus line (d)If time-out diagnosis codes associated with ECUs C and D are stored in ECUs A and B, or time-out codes associated with ECUs A and B are stored in ECUs C and D, CAN bus line (d) is suspected. CAN bus line (g) or (e) and power supply systems to ECU C or D are also suspected as second cause.
Time-out diagnosis codes associated with ECUs A and B are stored in ECU C and ECU D.

54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > TROUBLESHOOTING<CAN> > CAN BUS DIAGNOSIS > DIAGNOSIS ITEM 1
Diagnosis Item 1: Communication with no ECUs is possible (CAN-C).
 
 
cautionWhen servicing a CAN bus line, earth yourself by touching a metal object such as an unpainted water pipe. If you fail to do, a component connected to the CAN bus line may be broken.
 
 
TROUBLESHOOTING HINTS
  • Malfunction in CAN bus line (short to earth or power supply, wire short to one another)
  • Malfunction in the ECUs which are interconnected via CAN bus line (internal error)
  • Malfunction (open circuit) of wiring harness, connector(s) between the diagnosis connector and joint connector(s)
 
 
DIAGNOSIS PROCEDURE
STEP 1. Check the CAN bus lines for short to power supply. Voltage measurement at diagnosis connector.
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
(1) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(2) Voltage between diagnosis connector terminal No. 6 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(3) Voltage between diagnosis connector terminal No. 14 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
YES <Voltage is 4.0 V or less in both CAN_H and CAN_L> : Go to Step 2.
NO <Voltage is more than 4.0 V in either CAN_H or CAN_L> : Perform diagnosis item 2 "Diagnose shorts in the power supply to CAN bus line (CAN-C)". Refer to <LHD> or <RHD>.
 
STEP 2. Check the CAN bus lines for short to earth. Resistance measurement at diagnosis connector.
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
(1) Turn the ignition switch to the "LOCK" (OFF) position.
(2) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(3) Resistance between diagnosis connector terminal No. 6 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
(4) Resistance between diagnosis connector terminal No. 14 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
YES <Resistance value is 1 kΩ or more in both CAN_H and CAN_L> : Go to Step 3.
NO <Resistance value is less than 1 kΩ in either CAN_H or CAN_L> : Perform diagnosis item 3 "Diagnose shorts in the earth to CAN bus line (CAN-C)". Refer to <LHD> or <RHD>.
 
STEP 3. Check the CAN bus lines for short to each other. Resistance measurement at diagnosis connector.
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
(1) Turn the ignition switch to the "LOCK" (OFF) position.
(2) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(3) Resistance between diagnosis connector terminal Nos. 6 and 14
OK: 60 ± 10 Ω
Is the check result normal?
YES : The trouble can be an intermittent malfunction (Refer to GROUP 00 - How to Cope with Intermittent Malfunction ).
NO <Resistance value is less than 60 ± 10 Ω> : Perform diagnosis Item 4 "Diagnose shorts between CAN_H and L lines (CAN-C)". Refer to <LHD> or <RHD>.
NO <Resistance value is 1 kΩ or more> : Check the wires between diagnosis connector and joint connector (CAN1) for open circuit, and check the terminal resistors in the engine-ECU and the ETACS-ECU for open circuit. Then repair or replace if necessary.
 
54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > TROUBLESHOOTING<CAN> > CAN BUS DIAGNOSIS > DIAGNOSIS ITEM 2<LHD>
Diagnosis Item 2: Diagnose shorts in the power supply to CAN bus line (CAN-C). <LHD>
 
 
cautionWhen servicing a CAN bus line, earth yourself by touching a metal object such as an unpainted water pipe. If you fail to do, a component connected to the CAN bus line may be broken.
 
 
TROUBLE JUDGEMENT CONDITIONS
The M.U.T.-III judges the trouble when it is impossible to receive the periodically sent data and the voltage of CAN_H or CAN_L line is more than 4.0 V.
 
 
TROUBLESHOOTING HINTS
  • Malfunction of the wiring harness
  • Malfunction of the connector
  • Malfunction of the ETACS-ECU
  • Malfunction of the combination meter
  • Malfunction of the transfer-ECU <4WD>
  • Malfunction of the KOS&OSS-ECU <Vehicles with KOS>
  • Malfunction of the SRS-ECU
  • Malfunction of the ASTC-ECU
  • Malfunction of the A/T-ECU <A/T>
  • Malfunction of the AS&G-ECU <Vehicles with AS&G system>
  • Malfunction of the emergency call control unit <Vehicles with ERA-GLONASS system>
  • Malfunction of the FCM/LDW/AHB-ECU <Vehicles with FCM/LDW/AHB-ECU>
  • Malfunction of the engine-ECU
  • Malfunction of the steering wheel sensor (column switch assembly)
  • Malfunction of the clearance warning control unit <Vehicles with corner sensor system>
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for BSW) <Vehicles with Blind Spot Warning [BSW] (with Lane Change Assist) system>
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) <Vehicles with gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C)>
 
 
DIAGNOSIS PROCEDURE
STEP 1. Check the CAN bus lines. Voltage measurement at diagnosis connector.
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
noteThis inspection allows you to check that there is a short to power supply in either CAN_H line or CAN_L line. Thus, in the following steps, check the CAN bus line that is defective.
(1) Disconnect engine-ECU connector and ETACS-ECU connector, and measure the voltage at the harness side of diagnosis connector.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between diagnosis connector terminal No. 6 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Voltage between diagnosis connector terminal No. 14 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
<Both of the measurement results show 4.0 V or less> Go to Step 45.
<Either of CAN_H line or CAN_L line measurement result shows more than 4.0 V> Go to Step 2.
 
STEP 2. Check the CAN line. Voltage measurement at joint connector (CAN1).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN1), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between joint connector (CAN1) terminal No. 7 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Voltage between joint connector (CAN1) terminal No. 18 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
<4.0 V or less> Go to Step 25.
<More than 4.0 V> Go to Step 3.
 
STEP 3. Check the CAN line between joint connector (CAN2) and the engine-ECU. Voltage measurement at joint connector (CAN2).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN2), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 10 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Voltage between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 21 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
YES <Vehicles without ERA-GLONASS system> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 7.
YES <Vehicles with ERA-GLONASS system> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 4.
<More than 4.0 V> Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN2) and the engine-ECU connector.
 
STEP 4. Check the CAN line between joint connector (CAN2) and the emergency call control unit. Voltage measurement at joint connector (CAN2).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN2), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 1 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Voltage between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 12 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
<4.0 V or less> Go to Step 7.
<More than 4.0 V> Go to Step 5.
 
STEP 5. M.U.T.-III CAN bus diagnostics (emergency call control unit connector disconnected)
cautionStrictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Disconnect emergency call control unit connector, and diagnose by using the M.U.T.-III.
(2) Diagnose CAN bus lines, and check if M.U.T.-III screen is as shown in the illustration.
Does M.U.T.-III screen correspond to the illustration?
Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN2) and the emergency call control unit connector.
Check the emergency call control unit connector, and repair if necessary. If the emergency call control unit connector is in good condition, go to Step 6.
 
STEP 6. M.U.T.-III CAN bus diagnostics (retest the system)
Diagnose CAN bus lines, and check if M.U.T.-III screen shows normal state.
Is the check result normal?
The trouble can be an intermittent malfunction (Refer to GROUP 00 - How to Cope with Intermittent Malfunction ).
Check the emergency call control unit connector, and repair if necessary. If the emergency call control unit connector is in good condition, replace the emergency call control unit (Refer to GROUP 54A - Emergency Call Control Unit ).
 
STEP 7. Check the CAN line between joint connector (CAN2) and the ASTC-ECU. Voltage measurement at joint connector (CAN2).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN2), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 5 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Voltage between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 16 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
YES <Vehicles without KOS and Blind Spot Warning [BSW] (with Lane Change Assist) system> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 16.
YES <Vehicles without KOS and with Blind Spot Warning [BSW] (with Lane Change Assist) system> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 13.
YES <Vehicles with KOS> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 10.
<More than 4.0 V> Go to Step 8.

54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > TROUBLESHOOTING<CAN> > CAN BUS DIAGNOSIS > DIAGNOSIS ITEM 2<RHD>
Diagnosis Item 2: Diagnose shorts in the power supply to CAN bus line (CAN-C). <RHD>
 
 
cautionWhen servicing a CAN bus line, earth yourself by touching a metal object such as an unpainted water pipe. If you fail to do, a component connected to the CAN bus line may be broken.
 
 
TROUBLE JUDGEMENT CONDITIONS
The M.U.T.-III judges the trouble when it is impossible to receive the periodically sent data and the voltage of CAN_H or CAN_L line is more than 4.0 V.
 
 
TROUBLESHOOTING HINTS
  • Malfunction of the wiring harness
  • Malfunction of the connector
  • Malfunction of the ETACS-ECU
  • Malfunction of the combination meter
  • Malfunction of the transfer-ECU <4WD>
  • Malfunction of the KOS&OSS-ECU <Vehicles with KOS>
  • Malfunction of the SRS-ECU
  • Malfunction of the ASTC-ECU
  • Malfunction of the A/T-ECU <A/T>
  • Malfunction of the AS&G-ECU <Vehicles with AS&G system>
  • Malfunction of the FCM/LDW/AHB-ECU <Vehicles with FCM/LDW/AHB-ECU>
  • Malfunction of the engine-ECU
  • Malfunction of the steering wheel sensor (column switch assembly)
  • Malfunction of the clearance warning control unit <Vehicles with corner sensor system>
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for BSW) <Vehicles with Blind Spot Warning [BSW] (with Lane Change Assist) system>
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) <Vehicles with gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C)>
 
 
DIAGNOSIS PROCEDURE
STEP 1. Check the CAN bus lines. Voltage measurement at diagnosis connector.
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
noteThis inspection allows you to check that there is a short to power supply in either CAN_H line or CAN_L line. Thus, in the following steps, check the CAN bus line that is defective.
(1) Disconnect engine-ECU connector and ETACS-ECU connector, and measure the voltage at the harness side of diagnosis connector.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between diagnosis connector terminal No. 6 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Voltage between diagnosis connector terminal No. 14 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
<Both of the measurement results show 4.0 V or less> Go to Step 42.
<Either of CAN_H line or CAN_L line measurement result shows more than 4.0 V> Go to Step 2.
 
STEP 2. Check the CAN line. Voltage measurement at joint connector (CAN2).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN2), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 10 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Voltage between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 21 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
<4.0 V or less> Go to Step 19.
<More than 4.0 V> Go to Step 3.
 
STEP 3. Check the CAN line between joint connector (CAN1) and the ETACS-ECU. Voltage measurement at joint connector (CAN1).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN1), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between joint connector (CAN1) terminal No. 11 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Voltage between joint connector (CAN1) terminal No. 22 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
YES <M/T (Vehicles without KOS and Blind Spot Warning [BSW] (with Lane Change Assist) system)> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 13.
YES <M/T (Vehicles without KOS and with Blind Spot Warning [BSW] (with Lane Change Assist) system)> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 10.
YES <M/T (Vehicles with KOS)> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 7.
YES <A/T> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 4.
<More than 4.0 V> Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN1) and the engine-ECU connector.
 
STEP 4. Check the CAN line between joint connector (CAN1) and the A/T-ECU. Voltage measurement at joint connector (CAN1).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN1), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between joint connector (CAN1) terminal No. 8 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Voltage between joint connector (CAN1) terminal No. 19 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
YES <Vehicles without KOS and Blind Spot Warning [BSW] (with Lane Change Assist) system> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 13.
YES <Vehicles without KOS and with Blind Spot Warning [BSW] (with Lane Change Assist) system> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 10.
YES <Vehicles with KOS> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 7.
<More than 4.0 V> Go to Step 5.
 
STEP 5. M.U.T.-III CAN bus diagnostics (A/T-ECU connector disconnected)
cautionStrictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Disconnect A/T-ECU connector, and diagnose by using the M.U.T.-III.
(2) Diagnose CAN bus lines, and check if M.U.T.-III screen is as shown in the illustration.
Does M.U.T.-III screen correspond to the illustration?
Check the intermediate connector, and repair if necessary. If the intermediate connector is in good condition, repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN1) and the A/T-ECU connector.
Check the A/T-ECU connector, and repair if necessary. If the A/T-ECU connector is in good condition, go to Step 6.
 
STEP 6. M.U.T.-III CAN bus diagnostics (retest the system)
Diagnose CAN bus lines, and check if M.U.T.-III screen shows normal state.
Is the check result normal?
The trouble can be an intermittent malfunction (Refer to GROUP 00 - How to Cope with Intermittent Malfunction ).
Check the A/T-ECU connector, and repair if necessary. If the A/T-ECU connector is in good condition, replace the A/T-ECU (Refer to GROUP 23C - A/T-ECU ).
 
STEP 7. Check the CAN line between joint connector (CAN1) and the KOS&OSS-ECU. Voltage measurement at joint connector (CAN1).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN1), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between joint connector (CAN1) terminal No. 9 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Voltage between joint connector (CAN1) terminal No. 20 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
YES <Vehicles without Blind Spot Warning [BSW] (with Lane Change Assist) system> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 13.
YES <Vehicles with Blind Spot Warning [BSW] (with Lane Change Assist) system> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 10.
<More than 4.0 V> Go to Step 8.
 
STEP 8. M.U.T.-III CAN bus diagnostics (KOS&OSS-ECU connector disconnected)

(1) Disconnect KOS&OSS-ECU connector, and diagnose by using the M.U.T.-III.

Does M.U.T.-III screen correspond to the illustration?
Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN1) and the KOS&OSS-ECU connector.

caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN2), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 9 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Voltage between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 20 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
<4.0 V or less> Go to Step 41.
<More than 4.0 V> Go to Step 39.
 
STEP 39. M.U.T.-III CAN bus diagnostics (gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector disconnected)
cautionStrictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Disconnect gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector, and diagnose by using the M.U.T.-III.
(2) Diagnose CAN bus lines, and check if M.U.T.-III screen is as shown in the illustration.
Does M.U.T.-III screen correspond to the illustration?
Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN2) and the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector.
Check the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector, and repair if necessary. If the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector is in good condition, go to Step 40.
 
STEP 40. M.U.T.-III CAN bus diagnostics (retest the system)
Diagnose CAN bus lines, and check if M.U.T.-III screen shows normal state.
Is the check result normal?
The trouble can be an intermittent malfunction (Refer to GROUP 00 - How to Cope with Intermittent Malfunction ).
Check the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector, and repair if necessary. If the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector is in good condition, replace the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) (Refer to ).
 
STEP 41. Check the CAN line between joint connector (CAN2) and the diagnosis connector. Voltage measurement at joint connector (CAN2).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN2), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 6 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: Less than 1.0 V
(4) Voltage between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 17 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: Less than 1.0 V
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
<Less than 1.0 V> The trouble can be an intermittent malfunction (Refer to GROUP 00 - How to Cope with Intermittent Malfunction ).
<1.0 V or more> Repair the diagnosis connector, or the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN2) and the diagnosis connector.
 
STEP 42. M.U.T.-III CAN bus diagnostics (ETACS-ECU connector disconnected)
(1) Disconnect ETACS-ECU connector and diagnose by using the M.U.T.-III.
(2) Diagnose CAN bus lines, and check if M.U.T.-III screen is as shown in the illustration.
Does M.U.T.-III screen correspond to the illustration?
Go to Step 44.
Check the ETACS-ECU connector, and repair if necessary. If the ETACS-ECU connector is in good condition, go to Step 43.
 
STEP 43. M.U.T.-III CAN bus diagnostics (retest the system)
Diagnose CAN bus lines, and check if M.U.T.-III screen shows normal state.
Is the check result normal?
The trouble can be an intermittent malfunction (Refer to GROUP 00 - How to Cope with Intermittent Malfunction ).
Check the ETACS-ECU connector, and repair if necessary. If the ETACS-ECU connector is in good condition, replace the ETACS-ECU (Refer to GROUP 54A - ETACS-ECU ).
 
STEP 44. M.U.T.-III CAN bus diagnostics (engine-ECU connector disconnected)
(1) Disconnect engine-ECU connector, and diagnose by using the M.U.T.-III.
(2) Diagnose CAN bus lines, and check if M.U.T.-III screen is as shown in the illustration.
Does M.U.T.-III screen correspond to the illustration?

54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > TROUBLESHOOTING<CAN> > CAN BUS DIAGNOSIS > DIAGNOSIS ITEM 3<LHD>
Diagnosis Item 3: Diagnose shorts in the earth to CAN bus line (CAN-C). <LHD>
 
 
cautionWhen servicing a CAN bus line, earth yourself by touching a metal object such as an unpainted water pipe. If you fail to do, a component connected to the CAN bus line may be broken.
 
 
TROUBLE JUDGEMENT CONDITIONS
The M.U.T.-III judges the trouble when it is impossible to receive the periodically sent data and the voltage of CAN_H or CAN_L line is less than 1.0 V.
 
 
TROUBLESHOOTING HINTS
  • Malfunction of the wiring harness
  • Malfunction of the connector
  • Malfunction of the ETACS-ECU
  • Malfunction of the combination meter
  • Malfunction of the transfer-ECU <4WD>
  • Malfunction of the KOS&OSS-ECU <Vehicles with KOS>
  • Malfunction of the SRS-ECU
  • Malfunction of the ASTC-ECU
  • Malfunction of the A/T-ECU <A/T>
  • Malfunction of the AS&G-ECU <Vehicles with AS&G system>
  • Malfunction of the emergency call control unit <Vehicles with ERA-GLONASS system>
  • Malfunction of the FCM/LDW/AHB-ECU <Vehicles with FCM/LDW/AHB-ECU>
  • Malfunction of the engine-ECU
  • Malfunction of the steering wheel sensor (column switch assembly)
  • Malfunction of the clearance warning control unit <Vehicles with corner sensor system>
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for BSW) <Vehicles with Blind Spot Warning [BSW] (with Lane Change Assist) system>
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) <Vehicles with gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C)>
 
 
DIAGNOSIS PROCEDURE
STEP 1. Check the CAN bus lines. Resistance measurement at diagnosis connector.
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
noteThis inspection allows you to check that there is a short to earth in either CAN_H line or CAN_L line. Thus, in the following steps, check the CAN bus line that is defective.
(1) Disconnect engine-ECU connector and ETACS-ECU connector, and measure the resistance at harness side of diagnosis connector.
(2) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(3) Resistance between diagnosis connector terminal No. 6 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
(4) Resistance between diagnosis connector terminal No. 14 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
<Both of the measurement results show 1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 45.
<Either of CAN_H line or CAN_L line measurement result shows less than 1 kΩ> Go to Step 2.
 
STEP 2. Check the CAN line. Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN1).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN1), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(3) Resistance between joint connector (CAN1) terminal No. 7 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
(4) Resistance between joint connector (CAN1) terminal No. 18 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
<1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 25.
<Less than 1 kΩ > Go to Step 3.
 
STEP 3. Check the CAN line between joint connector (CAN2) and the engine-ECU. Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN2).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN2), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(3) Resistance between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 10 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
(4) Resistance between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 21 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
YES <Vehicles without ERA-GLONASS system> : <1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 7.
YES <Vehicles with ERA-GLONASS system> : <1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 4.
<Less than 1 kΩ > Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN2) and the engine-ECU connector.
 
STEP 4. Check the CAN line between joint connector (CAN2) and the emergency call control unit. Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN2).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN2), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(3) Resistance between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 1 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
(4) Resistance between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 12 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
<1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 7.
<Less than 1 kΩ > Go to Step 5.

cautionStrictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Disconnect emergency call control unit connector, and diagnose by using the M.U.T.-III.
(2) Diagnose CAN bus lines, and check if M.U.T.-III screen is as shown in the illustration.
Does M.U.T.-III screen correspond to the illustration?
Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN2) and the emergency call control unit connector.

<Less than 1 kΩ > Go to Step 8.

54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > TROUBLESHOOTING<CAN> > CAN BUS DIAGNOSIS > DIAGNOSIS ITEM 3<RHD>
Diagnosis Item 3: Diagnose shorts in the earth to CAN bus line (CAN-C). <RHD>
 
 
cautionWhen servicing a CAN bus line, earth yourself by touching a metal object such as an unpainted water pipe. If you fail to do, a component connected to the CAN bus line may be broken.
 
 
TROUBLE JUDGEMENT CONDITIONS
The M.U.T.-III judges the trouble when it is impossible to receive the periodically sent data and the voltage of CAN_H or CAN_L line is less than 1.0 V.
 
 
TROUBLESHOOTING HINTS
  • Malfunction of the wiring harness
  • Malfunction of the connector
  • Malfunction of the ETACS-ECU
  • Malfunction of the combination meter
  • Malfunction of the transfer-ECU <4WD>
  • Malfunction of the KOS&OSS-ECU <Vehicles with KOS>
  • Malfunction of the SRS-ECU
  • Malfunction of the ASTC-ECU
  • Malfunction of the A/T-ECU <A/T>
  • Malfunction of the AS&G-ECU <Vehicles with AS&G system>
  • Malfunction of the FCM/LDW/AHB-ECU <Vehicles with FCM/LDW/AHB-ECU>
  • Malfunction of the engine-ECU
  • Malfunction of the steering wheel sensor (column switch assembly)
  • Malfunction of the clearance warning control unit <Vehicles with corner sensor system>
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for BSW) <Vehicles with Blind Spot Warning [BSW] (with Lane Change Assist) system>
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) <Vehicles with gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C)>
 
 
DIAGNOSIS PROCEDURE
STEP 1. Check the CAN bus lines. Resistance measurement at diagnosis connector.
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
noteThis inspection allows you to check that there is a short to earth in either CAN_H line or CAN_L line. Thus, in the following steps, check the CAN bus line that is defective.
(1) Disconnect engine-ECU connector and ETACS-ECU connector, and measure the resistance at harness side of diagnosis connector.
(2) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(3) Resistance between diagnosis connector terminal No. 6 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
(4) Resistance between diagnosis connector terminal No. 14 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
<Both of the measurement results show 1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 42.
<Either of CAN_H line or CAN_L line the measurement results show less than 1 kΩ> Go to Step 2.
 
STEP 2. Check the CAN line. Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN2).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN2), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(3) Resistance between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 10 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
(4) Resistance between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 21 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
<1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 19.
<Less than 1 kΩ > Go to Step 3.
 
STEP 3. Check the CAN line between joint connector (CAN1) and the ETACS-ECU. Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN1).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN1), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(3) Resistance between joint connector (CAN1) terminal No. 11 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
(4) Resistance between joint connector (CAN1) terminal No. 22 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
YES <M/T (Vehicles without KOS and Blind Spot Warning [BSW] (with Lane Change Assist) system)> : <1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 13.
YES <M/T (Vehicles without KOS and with Blind Spot Warning [BSW] (with Lane Change Assist) system)> : <1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 10.
YES <M/T (Vehicles with KOS)> : <1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 7.
YES <A/T> : <1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 4.
<Less than 1 kΩ > Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN1) and the ETACS-ECU connector.

54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > TROUBLESHOOTING<CAN> > CAN BUS DIAGNOSIS > DIAGNOSIS ITEM 4<LHD>
Diagnosis Item 4: Diagnose shorts between CAN_H and L lines (CAN-C). <LHD>
 
 
cautionWhen servicing a CAN bus line, earth yourself by touching a metal object such as an unpainted water pipe. If you fail to do, a component connected to the CAN bus line may be broken.
 
 
TROUBLE JUDGEMENT
When all of the following conditions are met, the M.U.T.-III determines that a short circuit is present between CAN_L and CAN_H lines.
  • The M.U.T.-III cannot receive the periodic transmission data from any ECUs.
  • The voltage between CAN bus lines (CAN_L and CAN_H lines) is 1.0 V or more, 4.0 V or less.
  • The resistance at CAN bus line (CAN_L and CAN_H lines) is 2 Ω or less.
 
 
TROUBLESHOOTING HINTS
  • Malfunction of the wiring harness
  • Malfunction of the connector
  • Malfunction of the ETACS-ECU
  • Malfunction of the combination meter
  • Malfunction of the transfer-ECU <4WD (except 5M/T)>
  • Malfunction of the KOS&OSS-ECU <Vehicles with KOS>
  • Malfunction of the SRS-ECU <Vehicles with SRS>
  • Malfunction of the ASTC-ECU
  • Malfunction of the A/T-ECU <A/T>
  • Malfunction of the AS&G-ECU <Vehicles with AS&G system>
  • Malfunction of the emergency call control unit <Vehicles with ERA-GLONASS system>
  • Malfunction of the FCM/LDW/AHB-ECU <Vehicles with FCM/LDW/AHB-ECU>
  • Malfunction of the engine-ECU
  • Malfunction of the steering wheel sensor (column switch assembly)
  • Malfunction of the clearance warning control unit <Vehicles with corner sensor system>
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for BSW) <Vehicles with Blind Spot Warning [BSW] (with Lane Change Assist) system>
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) <Vehicles with gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C)>
 
 
DIAGNOSIS PROCEDURE
STEP 1. Connector check: joint connector (CAN1)
cautionThe strand end of the twist wire should be within 10 cm from the connector.
When checking the joint connector, ensure that its wiring harness side and its short pins are not damaged.
Is the check result normal?
Go to Step 2.
Repair the defective connector.
 
STEP 2. Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN1).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN1), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Turn the ignition switch to the "LOCK" (OFF) position.
(3) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(4) Resistance between joint connector (CAN1) terminal Nos. 7 and 18
OK: 120 ± 20 Ω
Is the check result normal?
<Within 120 ± 20 Ω> Go to Step 20.
<Not within 120 ± 20 Ω> Go to Step 3.
 
STEP 3. Connector check: joint connector (CAN2)
cautionThe strand end of the twist wire should be within 10 cm from the connector.
When checking the joint connector, ensure that its wiring harness side and its short pins are not damaged.
Is the check result normal?
Go to Step 4.
Repair a defective connector or replace the joint connector.
 
STEP 4. Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN2).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN2), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Turn the ignition switch to the "LOCK" (OFF) position.
(3) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(4) Resistance between joint connector (CAN2) terminal Nos. 10 and 21
OK: 120 ± 20 Ω
Is the check result normal?
YES <Vehicles without ERA-GLONASS system> : <Within 120 ± 20 Ω> Go to Step 8.
YES <Vehicles with ERA-GLONASS system> : <Within 120 ± 20 Ω> Go to Step 6.
<Not within 120 ± 20 Ω> Go to Step 5.
 
STEP 5. Resistance measurement at engine-ECU connector.
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Remove the engine-ECU, and measure at the equipment side.
(2) Resistance between engine-ECU connector terminal Nos. 153 and 166 <4N14>
OK: 120 ± 20 Ω
(3) Resistance between engine-ECU connector terminal Nos. 108 and 109 <4N15>
OK: 120 ± 20 Ω
Is the check result normal?
<Within 120 ± 20 Ω> Check intermediate connector, and repair if necessary. If the intermediate connector is in good condition, repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN2) and the engine-ECU connector.
<Not within 120 ± 20 Ω> Check the engine-ECU connector, and repair if necessary. If the engine-ECU connector is in good condition, replace the engine-ECU (Refer to GROUP 13A - Engine-ECU <4N14> or <4N15>).

(4) Resistance between joint connector (CAN2) terminal Nos. 1 and 12

caution

<Less than 1 kΩ> Go to Step 17.

54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > TROUBLESHOOTING<CAN> > CAN BUS DIAGNOSIS > DIAGNOSIS ITEM 4<RHD>
Diagnosis Item 4: Diagnose shorts between CAN_H and L lines (CAN-C). <RHD>
 
 
cautionWhen servicing a CAN bus line, earth yourself by touching a metal object such as an unpainted water pipe. If you fail to do, a component connected to the CAN bus line may be broken.
 
 
TROUBLE JUDGEMENT
When all of the following conditions are met, the M.U.T.-III determines that a short circuit is present between CAN_L and CAN_H lines.
  • The M.U.T.-III cannot receive the periodic transmission data from any ECUs.
  • The voltage between CAN bus lines (CAN_L and CAN_H lines) is 1.0 V or more, 4.0 V or less.
  • The resistance at CAN bus line (CAN_L and CAN_H lines) is 2 Ω or less.
 
 
TROUBLESHOOTING HINTS
  • Malfunction of the wiring harness
  • Malfunction of the connector
  • Malfunction of the ETACS-ECU
  • Malfunction of the combination meter
  • Malfunction of the transfer-ECU <4WD>
  • Malfunction of the KOS&OSS-ECU <Vehicles with KOS>
  • Malfunction of the SRS-ECU
  • Malfunction of the ASTC-ECU
  • Malfunction of the A/T-ECU <A/T>
  • Malfunction of the AS&G-ECU <Vehicles with AS&G system>
  • Malfunction of the FCM/LDW/AHB-ECU <Vehicles with FCM/LDW/AHB-ECU>
  • Malfunction of the engine-ECU
  • Malfunction of the steering wheel sensor (column switch assembly)
  • Malfunction of the clearance warning control unit <Vehicles with corner sensor system>
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for BSW) <Vehicles with Blind Spot Warning [BSW] (with Lane Change Assist) system>
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) <Vehicles with gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C)>
 
 
DIAGNOSIS PROCEDURE
STEP 1. Connector check: joint connector (CAN2)
cautionThe strand end of the twist wire should be within 10 cm from the connector.
When checking the joint connector, ensure that its wiring harness side and its short pins are not damaged.
Is the check result normal?
Go to Step 2.
Repair the defective connector.
 
STEP 2. Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN2).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN2), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Turn the ignition switch to the "LOCK" (OFF) position.
(3) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(4) Resistance between joint connector (CAN2) terminal Nos. 10 and 21
OK: 120 ± 20 Ω
Is the check result normal?
<Within 120 ± 20 Ω> Go to Step 16.
<Not within 120 ± 20 Ω> Go to Step 3.
 
STEP 3. Connector check: joint connector (CAN1)
cautionThe strand end of the twist wire should be within 10 cm from the connector.
When checking the joint connector, ensure that its wiring harness side and its short pins are not damaged.
Is the check result normal?
Go to Step 4.
Repair a defective connector or replace the joint connector.

<Within 120 ± 20 Ω> Check intermediate connector, and repair if necessary. If the intermediate connector is in good condition, repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN2) and the engine-ECU connector.
<Not within 120 ± 20 Ω> Check the engine-ECU connector, and repair if necessary. If the engine-ECU connector is in good condition, replace the engine-ECU (Refer to GROUP 13A - Engine-ECU <4N14> or <4N15>).
 
STEP 18. Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN2).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN2), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Turn the ignition switch to the "LOCK" (OFF) position.
(3) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(4) Resistance between joint connector (CAN2) terminal Nos. 4 and 15
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
<1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 20.
<Less than 1 kΩ> Go to Step 19.
 
STEP 19. Resistance measurement at transfer-ECU connector.
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Remove the transfer-ECU, and measure at the equipment side.
(2) Resistance at transfer-ECU connector terminal Nos. 55 and 56
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
<1 kΩ or more> Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN2) and the transfer-ECU connector.
<Less than 1 kΩ> Check the transfer-ECU connector, and repair if necessary. If the transfer-ECU connector is in good condition, replace the transfer-ECU (Refer to GROUP 22A - Transfer-ECU <M/T> or GROUP 23C - Transfer-ECU <A/T>).

OK: 1 kΩ or more

54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > TROUBLESHOOTING<CAN> > CAN BUS DIAGNOSIS > DIAGNOSIS ITEM 5
Diagnosis Item 5: Communication with no ECUs is possible (GW-CAN-C). <Vehicles with automatic A/C>
 
 
cautionWhen servicing a CAN bus line, earth yourself by touching a metal object such as an unpainted water pipe. If you fail to do, a component connected to the CAN bus line may be broken.
 
 
TROUBLESHOOTING HINTS
  • Malfunction in GW-CAN-C bus line (short to earth or power supply, wire short to one another)
  • Malfunction in the ECUs which are interconnected via GW-CAN-C bus line (internal error)
  • Malfunction (open circuit) of wiring harness, connector (s) between the diagnosis connector and joint connector(s)
 
 
DIAGNOSIS PROCEDURE
STEP 1. Check the CAN bus lines for short to power supply. Voltage measurement at gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector.
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
(1) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(2) Voltage between gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal No. 6 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(3) Voltage between gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal No. 5 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
YES <Voltage is 4.0 V or less in both CAN_H and CAN_L> : Go to Step 2.
NO <Voltage is more than 4.0 V in either CAN_H or CAN_L> : Perform diagnosis item 6 "Diagnose shorts in the power supply to CAN bus line (GW-CAN-C)" (Refer to ).
 
STEP 2. Check the CAN bus lines for short to earth. Resistance measurement at gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector.
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
(1) Turn the ignition switch to the "LOCK" (OFF) position.
(2) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(3) Resistance between gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal No. 6 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
(4) Resistance between gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal No. 5 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
YES <Resistance value is 1 kΩ or more in both CAN_H and CAN_L> : Go to Step 3.
NO <Resistance value is less than 1 kΩ in either CAN_H or CAN_L> : Perform diagnosis item 7 "Diagnose shorts in the earth to CAN bus line (GW-CAN-C)" (Refer to ).
 
STEP 3. Check the CAN bus lines for short to each other. Resistance measurement at gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector.
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
(1) Turn the ignition switch to the "LOCK" (OFF) position.
(2) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(3) Resistance between gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal Nos. 5 and 6
OK: 120 ± 20 Ω
Is the check result normal?
YES : The trouble can be an intermittent malfunction (Refer to GROUP 00 - How to Cope with Intermittent Malfunction ).
NO <Resistance value is less than 120 ± 20 Ω> : Perform diagnosis Item 8 "Diagnose shorts between CAN_H and L lines (GW-CAN-C)" (Refer to ).
NO <Resistance value is 1 kΩ or more> : Check the wires between gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector and joint connector (CAN3) for open circuit, and check the terminal resistors in the A/C-ECU and the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) for open circuit. Then repair or replace if necessary.
 
54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > TROUBLESHOOTING<CAN> > CAN BUS DIAGNOSIS > DIAGNOSIS ITEM 6
Diagnosis Item 6: Diagnose shorts in the power supply to CAN bus line (GW-CAN-C). <Vehicles with automatic A/C>
 
 
cautionWhen servicing a CAN bus line, earth yourself by touching a metal object such as an unpainted water pipe. If you fail to do, a component connected to the CAN bus line may be broken.
 
 
TROUBLE JUDGEMENT CONDITIONS
The M.U.T.-III judges the trouble when it is impossible to receive the periodically sent data and the voltage of CAN_H or CAN_L line is more than 4.0 V.
 
 
TROUBLESHOOTING HINTS
  • Malfunction of the wiring harness
  • Malfunction of the connector
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C)
  • Malfunction of the A/C-ECU
  • Malfunction of the camera-ECU <Vehicles with multi around monitor>
  • Malfunction of the multivision display <Vehicles with smartphone link display audio>
 
 
DIAGNOSIS PROCEDURE
STEP 1. Check the CAN bus lines. Voltage measurement at gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector.
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
noteThis inspection allows you to check that there is a short to power supply in either CAN_H line or CAN_L line. Thus, in the following steps, check the CAN bus line that is defective.
(1) Disconnect A/C-ECU connector and gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector, and measure the voltage at the wiring harness side.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal No. 6 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Voltage between gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal No. 5 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
<Both of the measurement results show 4.0 V or less> Go to Step 10.
<Either of CAN_H line or CAN_L line measurement result shows more than 4.0 V> Go to Step 2.
 
STEP 2. Check the CAN line between joint connector (CAN3) and the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C). Voltage measurement at joint connector (CAN3).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN3), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between joint connector (CAN3) terminal No. 6 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Voltage between joint connector (CAN3) terminal No. 17 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
YES <Vehicles without multi around monitor and smartphone link display audio> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 9.
YES <Vehicles without multi around monitor and with smartphone link display audio> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 6.
YES <Vehicles with multi around monitor> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 3.
NO : <More than 4.0 V> Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN3) and the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector.
 
STEP 3. Check the CAN line between joint connector (CAN3) and the camera-ECU. Voltage measurement at joint connector (CAN3).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN3), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between joint connector (CAN3) terminal No. 5 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Voltage between joint connector (CAN3) terminal No. 16 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
YES <Vehicles without smartphone link display audio> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 9.
YES <Vehicles with smartphone link display audio> : <4.0 V or less> Go to Step 6.
<More than 4.0 V> Go to Step 4.
 
STEP 4. M.U.T.-III CAN bus diagnostics (camera-ECU connector disconnected)
(1) Disconnect camera-ECU connector, and diagnose by using the M.U.T.-III.
(2) Diagnose CAN bus lines, and check if M.U.T.-III screen is as shown in the illustration.
Does M.U.T.-III screen correspond to the illustration?
Check the intermediate connector, and repair if necessary. If the intermediate connector is in good condition, repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN3) and the camera-ECU connector.
Check the camera-ECU connector, and repair if necessary. If the camera-ECU connector is in good condition, go to Step 5.
 
STEP 5. M.U.T.-III CAN bus diagnostics (retest the system)
Diagnose CAN bus lines, and check if M.U.T.-III screen shows normal state.
Is the check result normal?
The trouble can be an intermittent malfunction (Refer to GROUP 00 - How to Cope with Intermittent Malfunction ).
Check the camera-ECU connector, and repair if necessary. If the camera-ECU connector is in good condition, replace the camera-ECU (Refer to GROUP 54A - Camera-ECU ).
 
STEP 6. Check the CAN line between joint connector (CAN3) and the multivision display. Voltage measurement at joint connector (CAN3).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN3), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between joint connector (CAN3) terminal No. 4 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Voltage between joint connector (CAN3) terminal No. 15 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
<4.0 V or less> Go to Step 9.
<More than 4.0 V> Go to Step 7.
 
STEP 7. M.U.T.-III CAN bus diagnostics (multivision display connector disconnected)
(1) Disconnect multivision display connector, and diagnose by using the M.U.T.-III.
(2) Diagnose CAN bus lines, and check if M.U.T.-III screen is as shown in the illustration.
Does M.U.T.-III screen correspond to the illustration?
Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN3) and the multivision display connector.
Check the multivision display connector, and repair if necessary. If the multivision display connector is in good condition, go to Step 8.

Diagnose CAN bus lines, and check if M.U.T.-III screen shows normal state.

caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.

  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN3), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Connect the negative battery terminal, and turn the ignition switch to the "ON" position.
(3) Voltage between joint connector (CAN3) terminal No. 7 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(4) Voltage between joint connector (CAN3) terminal No. 18 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 4.0 V or less
(5) Disconnect the negative battery terminal.
Is the check result normal?
<4.0 V or less> Repair joint connector (CAN3).
NO : <More than 4.0 V> Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN3) and the A/C-ECU connector.
 
STEP 10. M.U.T.-III CAN bus diagnostics (A/C-ECU connector disconnected)

54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > TROUBLESHOOTING<CAN> > CAN BUS DIAGNOSIS > DIAGNOSIS ITEM 7
Diagnosis Item 7: Diagnose shorts in the earth to CAN bus line (GW-CAN-C). <Vehicles with automatic A/C>
 
 
cautionWhen servicing a CAN bus line, earth yourself by touching a metal object such as an unpainted water pipe. If you fail to do, a component connected to the CAN bus line may be broken.
 
 
TROUBLE JUDGEMENT CONDITIONS
The M.U.T.-III judges the trouble when it is impossible to receive the periodically sent data and the resistance of CAN_H or CAN_L line is less than 1.0 V.
 
 
TROUBLESHOOTING HINTS
  • Malfunction of the wiring harness
  • Malfunction of the connector
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C)
  • Malfunction of the A/C-ECU
  • Malfunction of the camera-ECU <Vehicles with multi around monitor>
  • Malfunction of the multivision display <Vehicles with smartphone link display audio>
 
 
DIAGNOSIS PROCEDURE
STEP 1. Check the CAN bus lines. Resistance measurement at gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector.
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
noteThis inspection allows you to check that there is a short to power supply in either CAN_H line or CAN_L line. Thus, in the following steps, check the CAN bus line that is defective.
(1) Disconnect A/C-ECU connector and gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector, and measure the resistance at the wiring harness side.
(2) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(3) Resistance between gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal No. 6 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
(4) Resistance between gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal No. 5 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
<Both of the measurement results show 1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 10.
<Either of CAN_H line or CAN_L line the measurement results show less than 1 kΩ> Go to Step 2.
 
STEP 2. Check the CAN line between joint connector (CAN3) and the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C). Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN3).
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN3), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(3) Resistance between joint connector (CAN3) terminal No. 6 (CAN_H) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
(4) Resistance between joint connector (CAN3) terminal No. 17 (CAN_L) and body earth
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
YES <Vehicles without multi around monitor and smartphone link display audio> : <1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 9.
YES <Vehicles without multi around monitor and with smartphone link display audio> : <1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 6.
YES <Vehicles with multi around monitor> : <1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 3.
<Less than 1 kΩ> Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN3) and the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector.

caution

54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > TROUBLESHOOTING<CAN> > CAN BUS DIAGNOSIS > DIAGNOSIS ITEM 8
Diagnosis Item 8: Diagnose shorts between CAN_H and L lines (GW-CAN-C). <Vehicles with automatic A/C>
 
 
cautionWhen servicing a CAN bus line, earth yourself by touching a metal object such as an unpainted water pipe. If you fail to do, a component connected to the CAN bus line may be broken.
 
 
TROUBLE JUDGEMENT
When all of the following conditions are met, the M.U.T.-III determines that a short circuit is present between CAN_L and CAN_H lines.
  • The M.U.T.-III cannot receive the periodic transmission data from any ECUs.
  • The voltage between CAN sub bus lines (CAN_L and CAN_H lines) is 1.0 V or more, 4.0 V or less.
  • The resistance at CAN sub bus line (CAN_L and CAN_H lines) is 2 Ω or less.
 
 
TROUBLESHOOTING HINTS
  • Malfunction of the wiring harness
  • Malfunction of the connector
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C)
  • Malfunction of the A/C-ECU
  • Malfunction of the camera-ECU <Vehicles with multi around monitor>
  • Malfunction of the multivision display <Vehicles with smartphone link display audio>
 
 
DIAGNOSIS PROCEDURE
STEP 1. Connector check: joint connector (CAN3)
cautionThe strand end of the twist wire should be within 10 cm from the connector.
When checking the joint connector, ensure that its wiring harness side and its short pins are not damaged.
Is the check result normal?
Go to Step 2.
Repair a defective connector or replace the joint connector.
 
STEP 2. Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN3)
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN3), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Turn the ignition switch to the "LOCK" (OFF) position.
(3) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(4) Resistance between joint connector (CAN3) terminal Nos. 6 and 17.
OK: 120 ± 20 Ω
Is the check result normal?
YES <Vehicles without multi around monitor and smartphone link display audio> : <Within 120 ± 20 Ω> Go to Step 8.
YES <Vehicles without multi around monitor and with smartphone link display audio> : <Within 120 ± 20 Ω> Go to Step 6.
YES <Vehicles with multi around monitor> : <Within 120 ± 20 Ω> Go to Step 4.
NO : <Not within 120 ± 20 Ω> Go to Step 3.
 
STEP 3. Resistance measurement at gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Remove the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C), and measure at the equipment side.
(2) Resistance between gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal Nos. 5 and 6
OK: 120 ± 20 Ω
Is the check result normal?
<Within 120 ± 20 Ω> Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN3) and the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector.
<Not within 120 ± 20 Ω> Check the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector, and repair if necessary. If the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector is in good condition, replace the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) (Refer to ).
 
STEP 4. Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN3)
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN3), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Turn the ignition switch to the "LOCK" (OFF) position.
(3) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(4) Resistance between joint connector (CAN3) terminal Nos. 5 and 16.
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
YES <Vehicles without smartphone link display audio> : <1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 8.
YES <Vehicles with smartphone link display audio> : <1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 6.
<Less than 1 kΩ> Go to Step 5.
 
STEP 5. Resistance measurement at camera-ECU connector
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Remove the camera-ECU, and measure at the equipment side.
(2) Resistance between camera-ECU connector terminal Nos. 1 and 21
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
<1 kΩ or more> Check intermediate connector, and repair if necessary. If the intermediate connector is in good condition, repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN3) and the camera-ECU connector.
<Less than 1 kΩ> Check the camera-ECU connector, and repair if necessary. If the camera-ECU connector is in good condition, replace the camera-ECU (Refer to GROUP 54A - Camera-ECU ).
 
STEP 6. Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN3)
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN3), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Turn the ignition switch to the "LOCK" (OFF) position.
(3) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(4) Resistance between joint connector (CAN3) terminal Nos. 4 and 15
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
<1 kΩ or more> Go to Step 8.
<Less than 1 kΩ> Go to Step 7.
 
STEP 7. Resistance measurement at multivision display connector
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Remove the multivision display, and measure at the equipment side.
(2) Resistance between multivision display connector terminal Nos. 3 and 13
OK: 1 kΩ or more
Is the check result normal?
<1 kΩ or more> Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN3) and the multivision display connector.
<Less than 1 kΩ> Check the multivision display connector, and repair if necessary. If the multivision display connector is in good condition, replace the multivision display (Refer to GROUP 54A - Smartphone Link Display Audio ).
 
STEP 8. Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN3)
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN3), and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Turn the ignition switch to the "LOCK" (OFF) position.
(3) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(4) Resistance between joint connector (CAN3) terminal Nos. 7 and 18
OK: 120 ± 20 Ω
Is the check result normal?
<Within 120 ± 20 Ω> The trouble can be an intermittent malfunction (Refer to GROUP 00 - How to Cope with Intermittent Malfunction ).
<Not within 120 ± 20 Ω> Go to Step 9.
 
STEP 9. Resistance measurement at A/C-ECU connector
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.

<Not within 120 ± 20 Ω> Check the A/C-ECU connector, and repair if necessary. If the A/C-ECU connector is in good condition, replace the A/C-ECU (Refer to GROUP 55B - Heater Control Unit ).
 
 
54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > TROUBLESHOOTING<CAN> > CAN BUS DIAGNOSIS > DIAGNOSIS ITEM 9
Diagnosis Item 9: Diagnose when the M.U.T.-III cannot receive the data sent by gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C). <Vehicles with automatic A/C>
 
 
cautionWhen servicing a CAN bus line, earth yourself by touching a metal object such as an unpainted water pipe. If you fail to do, a component connected to the CAN bus line may be broken.
 
 
FUNCTION
The diagnostic result demonstrates that "the M.U.T.-III cannot receive the sent data from the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C)" when the M.U.T.-III checks the periodically sent data from each ECU and cannot receive the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) data only.
 
 
TROUBLE JUDGEMENT CONDITIONS
M.U.T.-III judges the trouble when the periodically sent data from gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) cannot be received.
 
 
PROBABLE CAUSES
  • Damaged harness wires and connectors
  • Power supply circuit malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C)
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C)
 
 
DIAGNOSIS PROCEDURE
STEP 1. Connector check: joint connector (CAN2) and gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector
cautionThe strand end of the twist wire should be within 10 cm from the connector.
When checking the joint connector, ensure that its wiring harness side and its short pins are not damaged.
Is the check result normal?
Go to Step 2.
Repair the defective connector. Replace the joint connector as necessary.
 
STEP 2. Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN2) and gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN2) and the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector, and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Turn the ignition switch to the "LOCK" (OFF) position.
(3) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(4) Continuity between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 11 and gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal No. 3 <LHD>
OK: Continuity (2 Ω or less)
(5) Continuity between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 22 and gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal No. 2 <LHD>
OK: Continuity (2 Ω or less)
(6) Continuity between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 9 and gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal No. 3 <RHD>
OK: Continuity (2 Ω or less)
(7) Continuity between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 20 and gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal No. 2 <RHD>
OK: Continuity (2 Ω or less)
Is the check result normal?
<All the resistances measure 2 Ω or less> Power supply to the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) may be suspected. Troubleshoot the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) (Refer to ).
NO : <Either or all of the resistances measure more than 2 Ω> Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN2) and the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector.
 
 
54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > TROUBLESHOOTING<CAN> > CAN BUS DIAGNOSIS > DIAGNOSIS ITEM 10

cautionWhen servicing a CAN bus line, earth yourself by touching a metal object such as an unpainted water pipe. If you fail to do, a component connected to the CAN bus line may be broken.
 
 
FUNCTION
The diagnostic result demonstrates that "the M.U.T.-III cannot receive the sent data from the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C)" when the M.U.T.-III checks the periodically sent data from each ECU and cannot receive the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) data only.
 
 
TROUBLE JUDGEMENT CONDITIONS
M.U.T.-III judges the trouble when the periodically sent data from gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) cannot be received.
 
 
PROBABLE CAUSES
  • Damaged harness wires and connectors
  • Power supply circuit malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C)
  • Malfunction of the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C)
 
 
DIAGNOSIS PROCEDURE
STEP 1. Connector check: joint connector (CAN2) and gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector
cautionThe strand end of the twist wire should be within 10 cm from the connector.
When checking the joint connector, ensure that its wiring harness side and its short pins are not damaged.
Is the check result normal?
Go to Step 2.
Repair the defective connector. Replace the joint connector as necessary.
 
STEP 2. Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN2) and gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN2) and the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector, and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Turn the ignition switch to the "LOCK" (OFF) position.
(3) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(4) Continuity between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 11 and gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal No. 3 <LHD>
OK: Continuity (2 Ω or less)
(5) Continuity between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 22 and gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal No. 2 <LHD>
OK: Continuity (2 Ω or less)
(6) Continuity between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 9 and gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal No. 3 <RHD>
OK: Continuity (2 Ω or less)
(7) Continuity between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 20 and gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector terminal No. 2 <RHD>
OK: Continuity (2 Ω or less)
Is the check result normal?
<All the resistances measure 2 Ω or less> Power supply to the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) may be suspected. Troubleshoot the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) (Refer to ).
NO : <Either or all of the resistances measure more than 2 Ω> Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN2) and the gateway-ECU (for GW-CAN-C) connector.
 
 
54 -CHASSIS ELECTRICAL > 54C-CONTROLLER AREA NETWORK (CAN) > TROUBLESHOOTING<CAN> > CAN BUS DIAGNOSIS > DIAGNOSIS ITEM 14
Diagnosis Item 14: Diagnose when the M.U.T.-III cannot receive the data sent by steering wheel sensor.
 
 
cautionWhen servicing a CAN bus line, earth yourself by touching a metal object such as an unpainted water pipe. If you fail to do, a component connected to the CAN bus line may be broken.
 
 
FUNCTION
The diagnostic result demonstrates that "the M.U.T.-III cannot receive the sent data from the steering wheel sensor" when the M.U.T.-III checks the periodically sent data from each ECU and cannot receive the steering wheel sensor data only.
 
 
TROUBLE JUDGEMENT CONDITIONS
M.U.T.-III judges the trouble when the periodically sent data from steering wheel sensor cannot be received.
 
 
PROBABLE CAUSES
  • Damaged harness wires and connectors
  • Power supply circuit malfunction of the steering wheel sensor
  • Malfunction of the steering wheel sensor
 
 
DIAGNOSIS PROCEDURE
STEP 1. Connector check: joint connector (CAN1) <LHD> or joint connector (CAN2) <RHD> and steering wheel sensor connector
cautionThe strand end of the twist wire should be within 10 cm from the connector.
When checking the joint connector, ensure that its wiring harness side and its short pins are not damaged.
Is the check result normal?
Go to Step 2.
Repair the defective connector. Replace the joint connector as necessary.
 
STEP 2. Resistance measurement at joint connector (CAN1) <LHD>, joint connector (CAN2) <RHD> and steering wheel sensor connector.
caution
  • A digital multimeter should be used.
  • The test wiring harness should be used.
  • When measuring the resistance, disconnect the negative battery terminal.
  • Strictly observe the specified wiring harness repair procedure.
(1) Disconnect joint connector (CAN1) <LHD> or joint connector (CAN2) <RHD> and the steering wheel sensor connector, and measure at the wiring harness side.
(2) Turn the ignition switch to the "LOCK" (OFF) position.
(3) Ensure that the negative battery terminal is disconnected.
(4) Continuity between joint connector (CAN1) terminal No. 6 and steering wheel sensor connector terminal No. 3 <LHD>
OK: Continuity (2 Ω or less)
(5) Continuity between joint connector (CAN1) terminal No. 17 and steering wheel sensor connector terminal No. 4 <LHD>
OK: Continuity (2 Ω or less)
(6) Continuity between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 7 and steering wheel sensor connector terminal No. 3 <RHD>
OK: Continuity (2 Ω or less)
(7) Continuity between joint connector (CAN2) terminal No. 18 and steering wheel sensor connector terminal No. 4 <RHD>
OK: Continuity (2 Ω or less)
Is the check result normal?
<All the resistances measure 2 Ω or less> Power supply to the steering wheel sensor may be suspected. Troubleshoot the steering wheel sensor (Refer to GROUP 35C - Troubleshooting <Steering wheel sensor> ).
NO : <Either or all of the resistances measure more than 2 Ω> Repair the wiring harness between joint connector (CAN1) <LHD> or joint connector (CAN2) <RHD> and the steering wheel sensor.
